---

### **At 9pm, hereâ€™s what youâ€™ve got:**

- **20 clones** = The total number of times your page/project (likely a GitHub repo or similar) was **downloaded or copied**. Could be by the same person multiple times.
  
- **17 unique clones** = Out of those 20, **17 came from different people** (or at least different devices/IPs). So, only 3 of those 20 were duplicates. That's solidâ€”it means it's not just one person hammering the clone button.

- **170 views** = The total number of **times your page has been viewed**.

- **3 unique visitors** = This is the head-scratcher, right? Because it means **only 3 actual people (or devices)** viewed it during that window.

---

### **So what gives? Why the weird math?**

A couple things are probably going on:

1. **Time windows donâ€™t align perfectly.**  
   GitHub (and similar platforms) separate clone data and view data into **different reporting windows**, sometimes with a delay. That could explain why youâ€™ve got high clone activity but low recent view counts.

2. **Some clones donâ€™t come from page visits.**  
   People (or scripts) can clone a repo directly using Git commands without ever opening the webpageâ€”**bypassing the â€œviewsâ€ counter** entirely.

3. **Bots and crawlers.**

4. **People return multiple times.**

### **Bottom Line:**
- **Clones = actual engagement.**
